Executor's Duty for Deceased's Missed Fasts: Feeding, Not Fasting
Explaining executor's duties and worship classification

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on missed bodily acts of worship after death and distinguish between bodily, financial, and mixed acts regarding the executor's duty.

Core Idea
No one can fast or pray for the dead; only feeding compensates for missed bodily acts of worship.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq explains the crucial distinction in Hanafi law between different categories of worship when a person dies with missed obligations. Bodily acts like fasting and prayer cannot be performed by proxy—the executor must instead feed for each missed act. Financial acts are simply deducted from the estate, and mixed acts like hajj require sending a substitute. Understanding this tripartite division is essential for proper estate administration.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The passage rules that for missed fasts and prayers, the guardian does not fast or pray on behalf, but must feed (half a sa' per day or equivalent).
Note that the ruling applies to all bodily acts of worship.
2
Locate the dalil
The hadith from Sunan al-Nasa'i: 'No one can fast for anyone else and no one can pray for anyone else.'
This is the primary textual evidence.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The hadith explicitly negates proxy fasting and prayer, implying that the only substitute is feeding, as feeding is not a bodily act but a financial compensation.
In Hanafi usul, a prohibition of proxy indicates the act is purely personal.
4
Apply the tripartite classification
The passage then extends the same reasoning to all rights of Allah, categorizing them into: bodily acts (feeding), financial acts (direct payment from estate), and mixed acts (hajj by proxy).
Examples: fasting and prayer = bodily; zakat = financial; hajj = mixed.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويعتبر كل صلاة بصوم يوم على الصحيح وإلى أن سائر حقوقه تعالى كذلك، مالياً كان أو بدنياً. و عبادة محضة أو فيه معنى المؤنة كصدقة الفطر، أو عكسه كالعشر، أو مؤنة محضة كالنفقات، أو فيه معنى العقوبة كالكفارات وإلى أن الولي لا يصوم عنه ولا يصلي لحديث النسائي «لا عن أحد ولا يصلي أحد أحد وقيدنا بكونهما أدركا عدة من أيام أخر إذ لو عن ماتا قبله لا يجب عليهما الإيصاء لما قدمناه لكن لو أوصيناه به صحت وصيتهما لأن صحتها لا تتوقف على الوجوب . كذا في البدائع. وأشار أيضاً إلى أنه لو أوجب على نفسه الاعتكاف ثم مات أطعم عنه لكل نصف صاع من حنطة لأنه وقع اليأس عن بالإطعام كالصوم في الصلاة كذا ذكره الولوالجي في فتاويه فالحاصل أن ما كان عبادة بدنية فإن الوصي يطعم عنه بعد موته عن كل واجب كصدقة الفطر، وما كان عبادة مالية كالزكاة فإنه يخرج عنه القدر الواجب عليه، وما كان مركباً منهما كالحج فإنه يحج عنه رجلاً من مال الميت . يوم أدائه فوقع القضاء
And [the ruling] applies to every [missed] prayer as it does to a day of fasting according to the correct view, and it is similar for all rights of Allah Almighty, whether financial or bodily, whether a pure act of worship or one that involves the meaning of maintenance like sadaqat al-fitr, or its opposite like ushr, or pure maintenance like expenses, or involves the meaning of expiation like kaffarat. And [it extends] to the fact that the guardian does not fast for him nor pray due to the hadith of al-Nasa'i: 'No one can fast for anyone else and no one can pray for anyone else.' And we restricted it to the case where they [the deceased] had the capacity to make up a number of other days; but if they died before [being able to make up], it is not obligatory for them to make a will, as we have mentioned. However, if they did make a will, their will is valid because its validity does not depend on obligation. Thus in al-Bada'i. He also indicated that if one obligated i'tikaf upon himself and then died, food should be given for each [missed day] half a sa' of wheat, because hope has been lost. As for feeding, it is like fasting in prayer. Thus mentioned by al-Walwaliji in his Fatawa. So the conclusion is: whatever is a bodily act of worship, the executor must feed for it after death for every obligatory [act], like sadaqat al-fitr. Whatever is a financial act of worship, like zakat, then the amount obligatory upon him is taken out [from the estate]. Whatever is a combination of both, like hajj, then a man performs hajj on his behalf from the estate of the deceased. ...
Source pages p. 499

Commentary
This passage deals with the obligations of the executor (wali) regarding missed acts of worship after death. The key ruling is that bodily acts of worship, such as fasting and prayer, cannot be performed by anyone else on behalf of the deceased. Instead, the executor must feed for each missed fast (and each missed prayer according to the correct view) with half a sa' of wheat or similar. This is based on the hadith: 'No one can fast for anyone else and no one can pray for anyone else' (reported by al-Nasa'i). However, this ruling is restricted to cases where the deceased had the opportunity to make up but did not. If they died before being able to make up, they are not required to have made a will, but if they did will it, the will is valid. The passage further distinguishes between different categories of worship: pure bodily acts (e.g., fasting, prayer) where feeding is required; pure financial acts (e.g., zakat) where the amount is taken from the estate; and mixed acts like hajj where a substitute can be sent. The ruling applies to all obligations that are rights of Allah. This distinction is crucial for estate administration: the executor must determine the type of missed worship and act accordingly.

Key Terms
الولي (al-waliy): The guardian or executor responsible for managing the estate and fulfilling the deceased's obligations.
الإطعام (al-iṭʿām): Feeding as a substitute for missed bodily acts of worship; specifically half a sa' per missed fast.
عبادة بدنية (ʿibādah badanīyah): A bodily act of worship that cannot be performed by proxy; includes fasting and prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what must the executor do for the deceased's missed obligatory fasts that had the capacity to make up but were not made up?
A) Fast these days on his behalf.
B) Pay fidya by feeding half a sa' for each day.
C) Pray for his pardon.
D) Nothing, because the obligation drops after death.

Key Takeaway
For missed bodily acts of worship like fasting and prayer, the executor must feed for each missed obligation; no proxy fasting or prayer is allowed.

Ruling for Pregnant and Breastfeeding Women: Fearing Harm, Fidyah Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on fidyah for pregnant/breastfeeding women

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for pregnant and breastfeeding women regarding fasting when fearing harm, and distinguish the positions of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn regarding fidyah.

Core Idea
Pregnant/breastfeeding women may break fast if they fear harm; only qada is required—no fidyah—per the mufta bihi view.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq addresses a common dilemma: when a pregnant or breastfeeding woman fears harm to herself or her child, may she break her fast? The answer is yes, but what compensation is required? Within the Hanafi school, there is a well-known dispute between Abu Hanifa and his two leading disciples, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani (the Sahibayn), over whether a fidyah (half a sa' per day) must be paid in addition to making up the missed fasts. We will examine the ruling, its evidence, and the operative position for fatwa.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its conditions
First, state the basic ruling: pregnant and breastfeeding women may break the fast (rukhsah) when they fear harm to themselves or the child. The condition is a predominant assumption (ghalabat al-zann) based on experience or a trustworthy Muslim physician.
The passage specifies that without such fear, breaking the fast is not permitted.
2
Analyze the intra-Hanafi dispute
Abu Hanifa holds that in addition to qada, the woman must pay half a sa' of wheat or similar per day as fidyah (considered fard). The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) hold that only qada is required, no fidyah. Understand the basis of each position.
The dispute is recorded in the Hanafi texts; later authorities (e.g., al-Hidayah, al-Bahr al-Ra'iq) prefer the Sahibayn's view.
3
Identify the evidence (dalil)
The passage cites a hadith: 'Indeed Allah has removed fasting and half the prayer from the traveler, and from the pregnant and breastfeeding a third of what was left' (or similar). This hadith, though ahad, is used to justify the permission to break the fast and the requirement of qada. The fidyah derives from another interpretation or qiyas.
The hadith is narrated by Abu Dawood, Tirmidhi, and others.
4
Understand the distinction from coercion (ikrah)
The passage contrasts this case with that of a person coerced to break the fast to save a child's life. In coercion, no excuse is granted because the coerced person is not commanded to protect the child; his action is due to pressure. In contrast, the pregnant/breastfeeding woman is commanded to protect the child (intentional command), so breaking the fast is itself a commanded act, and expiation would be inconsistent.
This distinction helps justify the permissibility without kaffarah.
5
Determine the mufta bihi and practical implication
The mufta bihi (relied-upon position) is that of the Sahibayn: no fidyah, only qada. Thus, a woman who breaks her fast out of fear must only make up the missed days later; she does not pay any expiation.
This is the operative ruling for fatwa today.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
جاء رمضان قدم الأداء على القضاء وللحامل والمرضع إن خافتا على الولد أو النفس يصوم أحد [؟]هم، ويؤدي عن كل وتر نصف صاع لأنه فرض عند الإمام. كذا في غاية البيان.

قوله: (وللحامل والمرضع إذا خالفنا على الولد أو النفس) أي لهما الفطر دفعاً للحرج ولقوله إن الله وضع عن المسافر الصوم وشطر الصلاة وعن الحامل والمرضع ثلث ما ترك ا هـ . فقد نص على جواز الإيصاء بذلك، وحينئذ فلا مانع من التوفيق بما مر والله تعالى أعلم. وبه يندفع ما في حاشية مسكين عن الأقصر أي من أن مرادهم بالقتل قتل الصيد لا قتل الصوم

قيد بالخوف بمعنى غلبة الظن بتجربة أو إخبار طبيب حاذق مسلم كما في الفتاوى الظهيرية على ما قدمناه لأنها لو لم تخف لا يرخص لها الفطر وإنما لا يجوز إفطاره بسبب خوف هلاك ابنه في الإكراه لأن العذر في الإكراه جاء من قبل من ليس له الحق فلا يعذر لصيانة نفس غيره بخلاف الحامل والمرضع، وهناك فرق آخر مذكور في النهاية. وأطلق المرضع ولم يقيدها ليفيد أنه لا فرق بين الأم والظئر ، أما الظئر فلأن الإرضاع واجب عليها بالعقد، وأما الأم فلوجوبه ديانة مطلقاً وقضاء إذا كان الأب معسراً أو كان الولد لا يرضع من غيرها، وبهذا اندفع ما في الذخيرة من أن المراد بالمرضع الظئر لا الأم فإن الأب يستأجر غيرها. وإنما قال إذا خافتا على الولد، ولم يقل كالقدوري إذا خافتا على أنفسهما أو ولدهما» لأنه لا يشمل المستأجر إذ لا ولد لها. كذا قيل، وقد قيل إنه ولدها من الرضاع لأن المفرد المضاف ، يعم، سواء كان مضافاً لمفرد أو غيره كما صرحوا به، فيشمل الولد الذي ولدته والذي أرضعته لأنه ولدها شرعاً وإن كان ولدها مجازاً لغة والواو في قوله «والمرضع» بمعنى «أو» لأن هذا الحكم ثابت لكل واحد منهما على الانفراد كذا في النهاية. والحامل هي التي في بطنها ولد والمرضع هي التي لها اللبن ولا يجوز إدخال التاء في أحدهما كما في «حائض» و «طالق» لأن ذلك من الصفات الثابتة لا الحادثة إلا إذا أريد الحدوث فإنه يجوز إدخال التاء بأن يقال حائضة الآن وغداً. كذا في غاية البيان. ولم أر من صرح بأن الحامل والمرضع إذا ماتا قبل أن يزول خوفهما على الولد أو على أنفسهما أنه لا يلزمهما القضاء كالمريض والمسافر لكن صرح في البدائع بأن للقضاء شرائط منها: القدرة على القضاء وهو بعمومه يتناول الحامل والمرضع فعلى هذا إذا زال الخوف أياماً لزمهما بقدره، بل ولا

وهناك فرق آخر مذكور في أن الحامل والمرضع مأمورة بصيانة الولد مقصوداً ولا يتأتى بدون الإفطار عند الخوف فكانت مأمورة أيضاً بالإفطار والأمر به مع الكفارة التي بناؤها على الزجر عنه لا يجتمعان بخلاف الإكراه فإن كل واحد غير مأمور قصداً بصيانة غيره بل نشأ الأمر هناك من ضرورة حرمة القتل والحكم يتفاوت بتفاوت الأمر القصدي والضمني قوله : (وقد قيل إنه ولدها من الرضاع الخ) قال في النهر : لا يخفى أن هذا إنما يتم أن لو أرضعته والحكم أعم من ذلك فإنها بمجرد العقد لو خافت على الولد جاز لها الفطر.
قوله : (والمرضع هي التي لها اللبن الخ) قال في النهر : المرضع هي التي شأنها الإرضاع وإن لم تباشر، والمرضعة هي التي في حال الإرضاع ملقمة ثديها الصبي وهذا الفرق مذكور في الكشاف.
(رواه أبو داود في كتاب الصوم باب ٤٤ الترمذي في كتاب الصوم باب ٢١. النسائي في كتاب الصيام باب ٥١ ٦٢ ابن ماجه في كتاب الصيام باب ۱۲ أحمد في مسنده (٤/ ٣٤٧).
If Ramadan comes, one gives precedence to adaa over qada. And for the pregnant and breastfeeding woman, if they fear for the child or themselves, they fast... and they pay for each half a sa' because it is fard according to the Imam. Thus in Ghayat al-Bayan.

He said: (And for the pregnant and breastfeeding woman if they fear for the child or themselves) meaning they may break the fast to repel hardship, and due to his statement: 'Indeed Allah has removed fasting and half the prayer from the traveler, and from the pregnant and breastfeeding [He] removed a third of what he left' [i.e., a portion]. So he has explicitly permitted the will [to pay fidyah] in that. And then there is no obstacle to reconciling [the various narrations], and Allah knows best. And with this, the objection in the margin of Miskin from al-Aqsar is repelled, namely that what they meant by killing is killing of game, not killing of... [unclear].

[The permission] is restricted to fear meaning predominant assumption based on experience or the report of a trustworthy Muslim physician, as in al-Fatawa al-Zahiriyya, as we have mentioned, because if she does not fear, she is not permitted to break the fast. And she is not allowed to break the fast due to fear of the destruction of her son in the case of coercion (ikrah), because the excuse in coercion comes from one who has no right, so she is not excused for protecting another's life, unlike the pregnant and breastfeeding woman. And there is another difference mentioned in al-Nihaya. And he [the author] used the absolute term 'murdi' (breastfeeding) and did not qualify it, indicating there is no difference between the mother and a wet nurse. As for the wet nurse, breastfeeding is obligatory upon her by contract; as for the mother, it is obligatory upon her by religious duty absolutely, and by judicial requirement if the father is poor or the child does not accept from anyone else. With this, the objection in al-Dhakhira that what is meant by murdi' is the wet nurse and not the mother is refuted because the father can hire someone else. And he [the author] only said 'if they fear for the child' and did not say as al-Quduri did 'if they fear for themselves or their child' because a hired woman has no child. So it is said. And it has been said that it is her child from breastfeeding, because a singular noun when made definite by idafah is general, whether it is added to a singular or plural, as they have clarified, so it includes the child she gave birth to and the child she breastfeeds because it is her child legally, even if it is her child metaphorically in language. And the waw in 'wal-murdi' means 'or' because this ruling is established for each of them individually. Thus in al-Nihaya. And 'hamil' is the one who has a child in her belly, and 'murdi' is the one who has milk. And it is not permissible to insert the ta' in either of them, like in 'ha'id' and 'taliq', because these are permanent attributes, not temporary, unless one intends temporariness and then inserting ta' is permissible, e.g., 'ha'idatan al-ana wa ghadan'. Thus in Ghayat al-Bayan. And I have not seen anyone explicitly state that if the pregnant and breastfeeding woman die before their fear for the child or themselves subsides, that they do not have to make up, like the sick and traveler. But in al-Bada'i' it is clarified that qada has conditions, including ability to make up, and it is general and includes the pregnant and breastfeeding woman. So if the fear subsides for some days, they must make up those days. And rather...

There is another difference mentioned: the pregnant and breastfeeding woman is commanded to protect the child intentionally, and that cannot be achieved without breaking the fast when fearing, so she is also commanded to break the fast. The command to break the fast and the expiation (kaffarah) which is built upon deterrence cannot coexist. In contrast, in the case of ikrah, each person is not intentionally commanded to protect the other, but rather the command arises from the necessity of the prohibition of killing. And the ruling varies with the intentional and incidental command. He said: (And it has been said that it is her child from breastfeeding...) In al-Nahr: it is obvious that this is only if she breastfed him, and the ruling is more general than that, because merely by contract if she fears for the child it is permissible for her to break the fast. He said: (And al-murdi' is the one who has milk...) In al-Nahr: al-murdi' is one whose nature is to breastfeed even if she does not directly do it, and al-murdhi'ah is the one who is currently breastfeeding and putting her nipple to the child's mouth. This distinction is mentioned in al-Kashshaf.
(Narrated by Abu Dawood in Kitab al-Sawm, chapter 44; al-Tirmidhi in Kitab al-Sawm, chapter 21; al-Nasa'i in Kitab al-Siyam, chapters 51-62; Ibn Majah in Kitab al-Siyam, chapter 12; Ahmad in his Musnad, 4/347.)
Source pages p. 499

Commentary
This passage covers the ruling for pregnant and breastfeeding women regarding fasting. The matn states: if they fear harm to themselves or the child, they may break the fast and must make up later, and according to Abu Hanifa they must also pay half a sa' per day. The commentary expands on this: the permission to break fast is conditional upon predominant fear (ghalabat al-zann) based on experience or a trustworthy Muslim physician. The proof is a hadith: Allah has lightened fasting and prayer for the traveler and also for the pregnant and breastfeeding woman. The commentator then addresses several issues: (1) The term 'murdi' includes both the mother and wet nurse, because the wet nurse has a contractual obligation and the mother has a religious obligation. (2) The phrase 'child' includes both biological and foster child due to the generality of idafah. (3) The distinction between this case and coercion (ikrah) is that the pregnant/breastfeeding woman is commanded to protect the child intentionally, so breaking fast is the commanded act, and expiation would be contradictory. In coercion, there is no such intentional command, so they are not excused. The commentary also notes that if these women die before the fear subsides, they are still liable for qada when they had ability. The important intra-Hanafi dispute is mentioned in the initial line: Abu Hanifa considers the fidyah fard, while the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) say only qada is required. The mufta bihi (relied upon) position is that of the Sahibayn: no fidyah, only qada. The practical implication is that a pregnant or breastfeeding woman who breaks the fast out of fear must only make up the missed days later; she does not need to pay any expiation.

Key Terms
الحامل (al-ḥāmil): A pregnant woman, one who has a child in her belly.
المرضع (al-murḍiʿ): A breastfeeding woman, whether mother or wet nurse. The term is a permanent attribute, hence no ta'.
الكفارة (al-kaffārah): Expiation; in the text, the fidyah of half a sa' is considered a kaffarah by some.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the mufta bihi (relied-upon) position in the Hanafi school, what must a pregnant or breastfeeding woman do if she breaks her fast out of fear for the child?
A) Only make up the missed fasts.
B) Make up the fasts and pay half a sa' per day.
C) Pay half a sa' per day as expiation.
D) Nothing, because she had a valid excuse.

Key Takeaway
The mufta bihi Hanafi position is that a pregnant or breastfeeding woman who breaks her fast out of genuine fear must only make up the missed days later, with no additional fidyah.

Sawm — Fasting
beginner
6 min
Qada of Ramadan Fasts: No Tawali, Tarakhi, and Priority of Adaa
Expansion on matn: no consecutiveness, tarakhi, and adaa priority.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the permissibility of delaying qada fasts and prioritize adaa over qada when Ramadan arrives, and explain the evidential basis from the Quran and Hanafi usul.

Core Idea
Qada of Ramadan fasts is not required to be consecutive nor immediate; it is permissible to delay until the next Ramadan, but then current fasts take precedence.

This passage clarifies the flexibility in making up missed Ramadan fasts. It explains that consecutiveness (tawali) is not obligatory, based on the absolute wording of the Quranic verse (2:184), and that the obligation is on tarakhi (permissive delay), meaning one may delay qada. However, when the next Ramadan arrives, one must prioritize the current fasts over qada. This distinction has important practical implications for how a Muslim schedules their make-up fasts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the issue
The passage addresses the ruling for making up missed Ramadan fasts (qada). The core question is whether qada must be performed consecutively and whether delay is allowed.
2
Understand the ruling
The Hanafi position is that consecutiveness is not a condition (shart) for qada; it is merely recommended (mustahabb). Moreover, the command for qada is on tarakhi – one may delay it to any time before death.
Tarakhi means the first possible time is not specified; delaying without sin is allowed until the time becomes constrained near death.
3
Locate the dalil
The primary proof is the Quranic verse: 'a number of other days' (Surah Al-Baqarah, 2:184). The absolute expression ('mutlaq') is invoked to show that no condition of consecutiveness is added.
A variant recitation by Ubayy ibn Ka'b adding 'consecutively' is not widely transmitted and thus does not restrict the absolute ruling.
4
Analyze the usul principle
In Hanafi usul, an absolute command (mutlaq) is acted upon as is until there is evidence to restrict it. Since the added 'consecutively' is not mashhur, it is not relied upon. This principle governs the ruling.
Compare with the case of kaffarah yamin where Ibn Mas'ud's recitation is mashhur and thus accepted.
5
Apply the practical consequences
Because qada is on tarakhi, one may perform voluntary fasts before completing qada (unlike if it were immediate). When the next Ramadan arrives, the current adaa fasts take precedence, and qada is postponed until after Ramadan. No fidya is due for delaying qada into the next year as long as one is able to fast.
This differs from qada of prayers, which must be done immediately (fawr) and cannot be delayed without excuse.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (وقضيا ما قدرا بلا شرط ولاء) أي لا يشترط التتابع في القضاء لإطلاق قوله تعالى ﴿فعدة من أيام أخر﴾ [البقرة: ١٨٤] والذي في قراءة أبي «فعدة من أيام أخر متتابعه غير مشهور لا يزاد بمثله بخلاف قراءة ابن مسعود في كفارة اليمين فإنها مشهورة فيزاد. كذا في النهاية والكافي. لكن المستحب التتابع. وأشار بإطلاقه إلى أن القضاء على التراخي لأن الأمر فيه مطلق وهو على التراخي كما عرف في الأصول. ومعنى التراخي عدم تعين الزمن الأول للفعل ففي أي وقت شرع فيه كان ممتثلاً ولا إثم عليه بالتأخير، ويتضيق عليه الوجوب في آخر عمره في زمان يتمكن فيه من الأداء قبل موته ولهذا قال أصحابنا : إنه لا يكره لمن عليه قضاء رمضان أن يصوم متطوعاً ولو كان الوجوب على الفور يكره له التطوع قبل القضاء لأنه يكره له تأخير الواجب عن وقته المضيق، ولهذا إذا أخر قضاء رمضان حتى دخل آخر فلا فدية عليه لكونها تجب خلفاً عن الصوم عند العجز ولم يوجد لقدرته على القضاء ولهذا قال: (فإذا جاء رمضان آخر قدم الأداء على القضاء لأنه في وقته وهو لا يقبل غيره ويصوم القضاء بعده ، وهذا بخلاف قضاء الصلوات فإنها على الفور ولا يباح التأخير إلا بعذر. ذكره الولوالجي
He said: (And they should make up what they missed without the condition of consecutiveness) meaning consecutiveness is not required in making up [fasts] due to the generality of His statement: 'a number of other days' [Al-Baqarah 184]. And what is in the recitation of Ubayy: 'a number of other days consecutively' is not widely known, so it is not relied upon, unlike the recitation of Ibn Mas'ud regarding the expiation of an oath, which is widely known and thus relied upon. Thus in al-Nihaya and al-Kafi. But consecutiveness is recommended. And he indicated by his absolute statement that making up is permissive (tarakhi), because the command is absolute, and absolute commands indicate permissibility (tarakhi) as established in usul. The meaning of tarakhi is that the first time for the action is not specified; so any time he begins, he is compliant and there is no sin for delaying. However, the obligation becomes constrained at the end of his life, at a time when he is able to perform it before his death. That is why our companions said: It is not disliked for someone who owes qada of Ramadan to perform voluntary fasts; if the obligation were immediate, it would be disliked for him to perform voluntary fasts before qada, because delaying an obligatory act from its constrained time is disliked. And that is why if he delays qada of Ramadan until another Ramadan enters, there is no fidya upon him, because fidya is a substitute for fasting when unable, and that does not exist here because he is able to make up. And that is why he said: (If another Ramadan comes, he should give precedence to the current fast over qada, because it is in its time and does not accept anything else, and he should make up afterward.) This is contrary to making up prayers, which must be done immediately and delay is not permitted except for an excuse. Mentioned by al-Walwaliji.
Source pages p. 500

Commentary
This passage is an expansion on the matn's ruling about making up missed fasts. The commentator explains that there is no requirement to perform qada in consecutive days, citing the Quranic verse 'a number of other days' which is absolute and does not specify tawali (consecutiveness). The recitation of Ubayy adding 'consecutively' is not widely transmitted (ghayr mashhur) and thus does not affect the ruling, unlike the recitation of Ibn Mas'ud for kaffarah yamin, which is widely accepted. Despite the lack of obligation, consecutiveness is recommended (mustahabb). The commentator further explains that the command for qada is on tarakhi (permissive delay), meaning one may delay it until a later time, but it becomes obligatory once there is time before death. This is evidenced by the fact that our Hanafi scholars do not consider it disliked for someone with qada to perform voluntary fasts; if qada were immediate (fawr), voluntary fasts would be disliked because they delay the obligatory. Additionally, if one delays qada until another Ramadan, there is no fidya because fidya is only when one is unable to fast, and here he is able. However, when Ramadan arrives, the current obligation (adaa) takes precedence over qada, because the current fast is in its specific time. This is different from qada of prayers, which must be done immediately (fawr) and cannot be delayed without excuse. This distinction is important for practical fiqh: one should prioritize performing the current Ramadan fasts over making up past missed ones, and only after Ramadan should one make up. This ruling is based on the absolute nature of the Quranic command and the principle that absolute commands imply permissibility (tarakhi) in Hanafi usul.

Key Terms
التراخي (al-tarakhi): The permissibility of delaying a wajib act without an immediate deadline; the command is not constrained to the first possible time.
التتابع (al-tawali): Consecutiveness; performing the qada days in a row without interruption.
القضاء (al-qada): Making up an obligatory act after its designated time has passed, due to an excuse.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, if a person delays qada of Ramadan until the next Ramadan enters, what is the ruling?
A) He must pay fidya for the delay.
B) He should fast the qada first, then the current Ramadan.
C) He should fast the current Ramadan first, then make up the qada.
D) The qada is waived because the new Ramadan has arrived.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, qada of Ramadan fasts is flexible: no consecutiveness required, delay is permissible, but when the next Ramadan arrives, adaa takes precedence.

Ruling for Pregnant and Breastfeeding Women: Conditions for Breaking the Fast
Explains the conditions for pregnant/breastfeeding women to break fast.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the condition of khawf for pregnant/breastfeeding women to break the fast and explain why their case differs from coercion.

Core Idea
Pregnant and breastfeeding women may break fast only with overwhelming fear of harm to self or child.

This lesson from al-Bahr al-Raʾiq details the concession (rukhṣa) for pregnant and breastfeeding women to break the fast. The key is khawf – a well-founded fear of harm. We will unpack the condition, see how it differs from coercion, and understand who qualifies.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its key condition
The passage states that breaking the fast is permitted only when there is khawf. Define khawf as an overwhelming probability (ghalabat al-ẓann) of harm, based on experience or a reliable Muslim doctor's report.
Without khawf, the concession does not apply.
2
Distinguish from coercion (ikrāh)
Note the contrast: in coercion, the excuse comes from the coercer, who has no right to cause the fast to be broken. Therefore, the coerced person may not break the fast to save another's life. But the pregnant/breastfeeding woman is directly commanded to protect the child, so her fear excuses her.
The underlying principle: the one with the duty to protect is excused.
3
Determine who is included (mother and wet nurse)
The author uses the term 'al-murḍiʿ' absolutely, without restriction, to include both the mother and the wet nurse. Review the reasoning: the wet nurse's duty is contractual, the mother's is religious and sometimes judicial.
This refutes a view from al-Dhakhīra that limits 'murḍiʿ' to the wet nurse.
4
Understand the definition of 'walad' (child)
The condition 'fear for the child' uses the singular definite noun in the construct state, which is general. It covers both biological and foster children (by suckling). The wāw in 'wal-murḍiʿ' means 'or', indicating the ruling applies to each individually.
Linguistic precision: 'walad' includes all children for whom the woman is responsible.
5
Analyze the consequence of death before fear ends
If the pregnant/breastfeeding woman dies while the fear persists, no qaḍāʾ is required. This is consistent with the rule for all excused persons: if the excuse persists until death, nothing is owed. However, if the fear subsides temporarily, qaḍāʾ becomes wajib for those days.
The source quotes al-Badāʾiʿ: conditions for qaḍāʾ include ability.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الصوم فصل في العوارض الصوم قيد بالخوف بمعنى غلبة الظن بتجربة أو إخبار طبيب حاذق مسلم كما في الفتاوى الظهيرية على ما قدمناه لأنها لو لم تخف لا يرخص لها الفطر وإنما لا يجوز إفطاره بسبب خوف هلاك ابنه في الإكراه لأن العذر في الإكراه جاء من قبل من ليس له الحق فلا يعذر لصيانة نفس غيره بخلاف الحامل والمرضع، وهناك فرق آخر مذكور في النهاية. وأطلق المرضع ولم يقيدها ليفيد أنه لا فرق بين الأم والظئر، أما الظئر فلأن الإرضاع واجب عليها بالعقد، وأما الأم فلوجوبه ديانة مطلقاً وقضاء إذا كان الأب معسراً أو كان الولد لا يرضع من غيرها، وبهذا اندفع ما في الذخيرة من أن المراد بالمرضع الظئر لا الأم فإن الأب يستأجر غيرها. وإنما قال إذا خافتا على الولد، ولم يقل كالقدوري إذا خافتا على أنفسهما أو ولدهما لأنه لا يشمل المستأجر إذ لا ولد لها. كذا قيل، وقد قيل إنه ولدها من الرضاع لأن المفرد المضاف يعم، سواء كان مضافاً لمفرد أو غيره كما صرحوا به، فيشمل الولد الذي ولدته والذي أرضعته لأنه ولدها شرعاً وإن كان ولدها مجازاً لغة والواو في قوله «والمرضع» بمعنى «أو» لأن هذا الحكم ثابت لكل واحد منهما على الانفراد كذا في النهاية. والحامل هي التي في بطنها ولد والمرضع هي التي لها اللبن ولا يجوز إدخال التاء في أحدهما كما في «حائض» و «طالق» لأن ذلك من الصفات الثابتة لا الحادثة إلا إذا أريد الحدوث فإنه يجوز إدخال التاء بأن يقال حائضة الآن وغداً. كذا في غاية البيان. ولم أر من صرح بأن الحامل والمرضع إذا ماتا قبل أن يزول خوفهما على الولد أو على أنفسهما أنه لا يلزمهما القضاء كالمريض والمسافر لكن صرح في البدائع بأن للقضاء شرائط منها: القدرة على القضاء وهو بعمومه يتناول الحامل والمرضع فعلى هذا إذا زال الخوف أياماً لزمهما بقدره، بل ولا خصوصية فإن كل من أفطر لعذر ومات قبل زواله لا يلزمه شيء فيدخل المكره والأقسام الثمانية المتقدمة.
Book of Fasting, Section on Excuses. Fasting is conditioned by fear, meaning overwhelming probability based on experience or information from a skilled Muslim doctor, as in al-Fatawa al-Zahiriyya, according to what we have mentioned, because if she does not fear, she is not permitted to break her fast. He may not break his fast due to fear of his son's destruction in the case of coercion, because the excuse in coercion comes from one who has no right, so he is not excused for protecting another's life, unlike the pregnant and breastfeeding woman. There is another difference mentioned in al-Nihaya. And he (the author) used the term 'al-murdiʿ' (breastfeeding) absolutely and did not restrict it, to indicate that there is no difference between the mother and the wet nurse. As for the wet nurse, because breastfeeding is obligatory upon her by contract; as for the mother, because it is obligatory as a religious duty absolutely, and judicially if the father is insolvent or the child will not suckle from another. And with this, what is in al-Dhakhira—that the intended meaning of 'al-murdiʿ' is the wet nurse, not the mother, because the father can hire someone else—is refuted. He only said 'if they fear for the child', and did not say like al-Quduri 'if they fear for themselves or their child' because it would not include the hired (wet nurse) as she has no child. It is said thus, and it has been said that it is her child by suckling, because the singular definite noun is general, whether it is added to a singular or other, as they stated, so it includes the child she gave birth to and the child she suckled, because it is her child legally, even if it is her child metaphorically in language. The 'waw' in 'wal-murdiʿ' means 'or', because this ruling is established for each of them individually, as in al-Nihaya. The pregnant woman is the one who has a child in her womb, and the breastfeeding woman is the one who has milk, and it is not permissible to insert the feminine 'ta' in either, as in 'Ha'id' and 'Taliq', because these are permanent attributes, not incidental, unless the incidental is intended, in which case inserting the 'ta' is permissible, such as saying 'Haidah now and tomorrow'. As in Ghayat al-Bayan. I have not seen anyone explicitly state that the pregnant and breastfeeding women, if they die before their fear for the child or for themselves disappears, that they do not have to make up (the fasts), like the sick and the traveler. But in al-Bada'i', it is stated that there are conditions for making up: among them, the ability to make up, and its generality includes the pregnant and breastfeeding women. So based on this, if the fear ends for some days, they owe (qada') for that many. Rather, there is no specificity; whoever breaks the fast due to an excuse and dies before the excuse disappears, nothing is incumbent upon him, including the coerced one and the eight previous categories.
Source pages p. 500

Commentary
This passage from 'al-Bahr al-Ra'iq' is a commentary on 'Kanz al-Daqa'iq' dealing with excuses (a'warid) for breaking the fast. The author explains the ruling for pregnant and breastfeeding women. The key condition is 'khawf' (fear), which is defined as an overwhelming probability based either on personal experience or the information of a skilled, upright Muslim doctor. Without this fear, the concession to break the fast is not permitted. The text distinguishes this case from coercion (ikrah): in coercion, the excuse arises from the person coercing, who has no right to cause the breaking of the fast, so the coerced person is not excused to protect another's life. In contrast, the pregnant or breastfeeding woman is directly commanded to protect the child, so her fear is a valid excuse. The author clarifies that 'al-murdiʿ' (the breastfeeding woman) includes both the mother and the wet nurse, as breastfeeding is obligatory for the mother in religious duty if the father is poor or the child refuses others, and for the wet nurse by contract. Thus, the mother is not excluded in favor of the wet nurse as some claimed. The definition of 'walad' (child) in the condition 'if they fear for the child' includes both biological and foster children through suckling, based on the principle that a definite singular noun in the construct state is general. The pregnant woman is defined as one with a child in her womb, and the breastfeeding woman as one who has milk, and the feminine ending 'ta' is not used because these are permanent attributes, not temporary. Finally, the text addresses the issue of death before the fear subsides: the author notes that he has not seen explicit statement that the pregnant/breastfeeding woman is exempt from qada' if she dies, but quotes from al-Bada'i' that the conditions for qada' include ability, so if the fear ends temporarily, she must make up those days. The concluding sentence states that anyone who breaks the fast due to an excuse and dies before the excuse is removed has no obligation (neither qada' nor fidya), which is a general rule applying to all excuses.

Key Terms
الخوف (al-khawf): Overwhelming probability (غلبة الظن) that harm will occur, based on experience or a reliable Muslim doctor's report.
الحامل (al-hāmil): A woman who has a child in her womb (pregnant).
المرضع (al-murḍiʿ): A woman who has milk, whether she is breastfeeding at the moment or not.
الإكراه (al-ikrāh): Coercion, where the excuse comes from the coercer, so the coerced is not excused for breaking fast to save another's life.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What condition must be met for a pregnant woman to be permitted to break her fast?
A) She must be in the first trimester.
B) She must have a doctor's general advice.
C) She must have an overwhelming probability (ghalabat al-zann) of harm based on experience or a reliable Muslim doctor's report.
D) She must be unable to find any food.

Key Takeaway
Pregnant and breastfeeding women may break the fast only when they have a well-founded fear of harm to themselves or the child, and they must make up missed fasts if the fear later subsides.

Fidya for the Permanently Incapacitated Elderly
Explains fidya for the decrepit elderly

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions under which an elderly person (shaykh fani) must pay fidya instead of making up missed fasts, and explain the role of 'continuation of inability' (istimrar al-'ajz) in the substitution ruling.

Core Idea
An elderly person who cannot fast pays fidya only; if ability returns, the fidya is void because substitution requires ongoing inability.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq explains the unique ruling for the shaykh fani, a person whose strength declines daily until death. Unlike others who miss fasts, the shaykh fani is not required to make them up (qada') but must pay fidya. The lesson explores the rationale, the conditions for the fidya, and the critical difference from tayammum regarding the continuation of the excuse.

Guided Path
1
Identify the subject and ruling
The shaykh fani is permitted to break fast and must pay fidya. This is based on a specific textual evidence (nas) that applies only to this category, not to the sick, traveler, pregnant, or breastfeeding.
The text says: 'He is permitted to break the fast due to difficulty, and his excuse is not a passing one that would lead to qada', so fidya is obligatory.'
2
Trace the proof
The proof is the Quranic verse (2:184) that allows fidya for those who can only do so with difficulty, but the Hanafi school restricts it to the permanently incapacitated. The passage states that no text came for others, but it came for the shaykh fani.
Evidence is 'ورود نص' (textual evidence) — the verse is implied.
3
Understand the condition of substitution
The fidya is a substitute (khalaf) for the fast. Its validity depends on the continuation of the inability (istimrar al-'ajz). If the person later becomes able to fast, the fidya is nullified because the condition for substitution is no longer met.
The text says: 'If he is able to fast, the ruling of fidya is nullified because the condition for substitution is the continuation of inability.'
4
Distinguish from tayammum
In tayammum, the substitution does not retroactively invalidate prayers performed with tayammum if water is found later. The reason is that the condition for tayammum is only the absence of water at the time, not its continuation, unlike fidya.
This contrast highlights the different ruling due to qiyas vs. specific evidence.
5
Apply to related cases
The text discusses other scenarios: a shaykh fani traveler, a person who vowed fasting and became unable, and one who missed fasts and became decrepit. All follow the same principle: fidya is due if the inability is permanent and the fast was originally obligatory on him.
The text clarifies that fidya is only for 'original' fasts (like Ramadan, qada', vows), not for kaffara fasts.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (وللشيخ الفاني وهو يفدى فقط) أي له الفطر وعليه الفدية وليست على غيره من المريض والمسافر والحامل والمرضع لعدم ورود نص فيهم، ووروده في الشيخ الفاني وهو الذي كل يوم في نقص إلى أن يموت وسمي به إما لأنه قرب من الفناء أو لأنه فنيت قوته، وإنما لزمته باعتبار شهوده للشهر حتى لو تحمل المشقة وصام كان مؤدياً، وإنما أبيح له الفطر لأجل الحرج وعذره ليس بعرض الزوال حتى يصار إلى القضاء فوجب الفدية لكل يوم نصف صاع أو صاعاً من تمر أو شعير كصدقة الفطر لكن يجوز هنا طعام الإباحة أكلتان من بر أو زبيب مشبعتان بخلاف صدقة الفطر كما قدمناه كذا في فتح القدير وفتاوى قاضيخان. وفي معراج الدراية : ولا يجوز في الفدية الإباحة لأنها تنبئ عن تمليك ا هـ. وهو مخالف لما قدمناه، ويحمل ما في المعراج على الفدية في الحج. ولو قدر على الصوم يبطل حكم الفداء لأن شرط الخلفية استمرار العجز في الصوم، وإنما قيدنا به ليخرج إذا قدر على الماء لا تبطل الصلوات المؤداة بالتيمم لأن خلفية التيمم مشروط بمجرد العجز عن الماء لا بقيد دوامه، وكذا خلفية الأشهر عن الأقراء في الاعتداد مشروط بانقطاع الدم من سن اليأس لا بشرط دوامه حتى لا تبطل الأنكحة الماضية بعود الدم على ما قدمناه في الحيض. وفي الكافي : وشرط الخلفية استمرار العجز كما في اليمين وفي صوم دم المتعة وغيرها قد تخلف لقيام الدليل ا هـ . وأشار المصنف فيما سبق من أن المسافر إذا لم يدرك عة فلا شيء عليه إذا مات إلى أن الشيخ الفاني لو كان مسافراً فمات قبل الإقامة لا يجب عليه الإيصاء بالفدية لأنه يخالف غيره في التخفيف لا في التغليظ لكن ذكره الشارحون بصيغة «قيل» ينبغي أن لا يجب مع أن الأولى الجزم به لاستفادته مما ذكرناه ولعلها ليست صريحة في كلام أهل المذهب فلم يجزموا بها، لأن الفدية لا تجوز إلا عن صوم هو أصل بنفسه لا بدل عن غيره فجازت عن رمضان وقضائه والنذر حتى لو نذر الأبد فضعف عن الصوم لاشتغاله بالمعيشة له أن يطعم ويفطر لأنه استيقن أن لا يقدر على قضائه وإن لم يقدر على الإطعام لعسرته يستغفر الله تعالى، وإن لم يقدر لشدة الحر كان له أن يفطر ويقضيه في الشتاء إذا لم يكن نذر الأبد. ولو نذر صوماً معيناً فلم يصم حتى صار فانياً جازت له الفدية، ولو وجبت عليه كفارة يمين أو قتل فلم يجد ما يكفر به وهو شيخ كبير عاجز عن الصوم أو لم يصم حتى صار شيخاً كبيراً لا يصح صومه لأن فرض الصوم وجب عليه، وليس عليه إلا أن يصوم مع القدرة فإذا عجز لم يبق في ذمته شيء فعليه الفدية فقط. ولو كان عليه صوم واجب فأفطر ولم يقض حتى صار فانياً، فعليه الفدية، وكذا لو كان عليه صوم نذر معين.
His statement: 'And for the decrepit old man (shaykh fani), he only gives compensation (fidya).' That is, he may break the fast and the fidya is upon him, and it is not upon others like the sick, traveler, pregnant, and breastfeeding woman, because no textual evidence came regarding them, while it came regarding the decrepit old man. He is the one who decreases every day until he dies; he is called by this name either because he is close to perishing (fana') or because his strength has perished. The fidya becomes incumbent upon him due to his witnessing the month, such that if he endures hardship and fasts, it is valid (ada'). He is permitted to break the fast due to difficulty, and his excuse is not a passing one that would lead to qada', so fidya is obligatory: for each day, half a sa' or a sa' of dates or barley, like sadaqat al-fitr, but here it is permissible to give in the form of ibaha (permission to eat two satiating meals of wheat or raisins), unlike sadaqat al-fitr, as we have mentioned earlier: this is in Fath al-Qadir and Fatawa Qadikhan. In Mi'raj al-Diraya: 'It is not permissible in fidya to give ibaha because it implies ownership (tamlik).' This contradicts what we have said, and it is interpreted as referring to fidya in Hajj. If he is able to fast, the ruling of fidya is nullified because the condition for substitution (khalafiyya) is the continuation of inability in fasting. We only restricted it with this to exclude the case of tayammum: if one becomes able to use water, the prayers performed with tayammum are not invalidated, because the substitution in tayammum is conditioned merely by the inability to use water, not by its continuation. Similarly, the substitution of months for periods (in 'idda) is conditioned by the cessation of blood from menopause, not by its continuation, so that past marriages are not invalidated by the return of bleeding, as we mentioned in hayd. In al-Kafi: 'The condition for substitution is the continuation of inability, as in the case of an oath, but in the fasting of tamattu' and others, it may differ due to evidence.' The author indicated previously that if a traveler does not reach [something?], he owes nothing if he dies, and that if the decrepit old man were a traveler and died before settling, he would not be required to make a will regarding fidya, because he differs from others in leniency, not in strictness. But the commentators mentioned it in the form of 'qila' (it is said), suggesting that it should not be obligatory, though it would be better to be certain of it based on what we have mentioned; perhaps it is not explicit in the words of the school's scholars, so they did not assert it. Because fidya is only permitted for a fast that is original in itself, not a substitute for another. Thus it is permissible for Ramadan, its qada', and vows. Even if one vowed perpetual fasting and became weak due to earning a living, he may feed and break his fast because he is certain he cannot make it up. If he cannot afford feeding due to poverty, he seeks forgiveness from Allah. If he cannot fast due to extreme heat, he may break and make it up in winter if he did not vow perpetual fasting. If one vowed a specific fast and did not fast until he became decrepit, fidya is permissible for him. If an expiatory fast (kaffara of oath or killing) becomes obligatory and he cannot find means to expiate, and he is an old man unable to fast, or he did not fast until he became a decrepit old man, his fast is not valid, but the obligation of fasting was upon him when able; when he becomes unable, nothing remains in his responsibility except fidya. If he had an obligatory fast (e.g., missed Ramadan) and did not make it up until he became decrepit, fidya is upon him. Similarly, if he owed a specific vowed fast.
Source pages p. 501

Commentary
This passage from 'al-Bahr al-Ra'iq' is the commentary on the matn statement 'And for the decrepit old man (shaykh fani), he only gives compensation (fidya).' The author explains that this ruling applies exclusively to the very old person whose strength declines daily until death. Such a person is permitted to break the fast, and instead of making up missed days (qada'), he must pay fidya: either half a sa' (about 1.6 kg) or a full sa' of dates or barley per day, similar to sadaqat al-fitr. However, unlike sadaqat al-fitr, the fidya can also be given as 'ibaha' (permission to eat two satiating meals of wheat or raisins), according to Fath al-Qadir and Fatawa Qadikhan, though there is a conflicting view from Mi'raj al-Diraya that restricts ibaha to fidya in Hajj. The key point is that the fidya is a substitute for the fast, and its validity depends on the continuation of inability (stavrar al-'ajz). If the old person recovers and becomes able to fast, the fidya is voided because the condition for substitution is the ongoing inability. The author contrasts this with tayammum, where the substitution does not lapse retroactively once ability returns. The text also addresses a subtle case: if the decrepit old man is also a traveler at the time of his death, there is a debate whether he must make a will for fidya; the preferred view is that he does not, as the concession for travel is leniency, not strictness. The passage further clarifies that fidya is only due for original fasts (like Ramadan, its qada', and vows) where the fast was obligatory on the person himself. For substitute fasts like kaffara, the ruling may differ. Finally, the author states that if someone was obligated to fast (e.g., missed days) and became decrepit before making them up, fidya is due. If he becomes decrepit after making a vow to fast on specific days, fidya is due for those days.

Key Terms
الشيخ الفاني (al-shaykh al-fānī): A very old person whose strength diminishes daily, nearing death. Also called 'fani' due to being close to perishing (fana') or having exhausted strength.
الفدية (al-fidya): Compensation paid for a missed fast, typically half or one sa' of staple food per day, given in tamlik (ownership) or ibaha (permission to eat).
الخلفية (al-khalafiyya): Substitution: the condition for a substitute ruling (e.g., fidya replacing fast) is the continuation of the cause (e.g., inability to fast).
الإباحة (al-ibāha): Giving permission to eat or use something; in fidya, it means inviting a poor person to eat two satiating meals, not transferring ownership.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
When does the fidya paid by an elderly person become void?
A) If he dies before paying it
B) If he recovers and becomes able to fast
C) If he travels
D) If he misses a day intentionally

Key Takeaway
An elderly person with a permanent inability to fast pays fidya instead of making up fasts, but the fidya is void if ability to fast returns.

Ruling for the Elderly Unable to Fast: Fidya
Explanation of fidya obligation for the elderly who cannot fast

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for the elderly who cannot fast, identify the condition for fidya, and explain the reasoning from textual evidence and qiyas.

Core Idea
The elderly with permanent inability pay fidya, not qada, because the text and analogy require sustained inability.

When age or chronic illness makes fasting permanently impossible, the obligation changes. The Hanafi school uniquely requires fidya (food compensation) without making up missed fasts. This lesson unpacks the ruling, its textual basis, and the principle of substitution (khilafah) that governs it.

Guided Path
1
Identify the subject and ruling
The passage discusses 'shaykh fani' (decrepit old person) who is allowed to break fast and must pay fidya. This ruling applies only when inability is permanent.
Distinguish from temporary excuses like travel or pregnancy.
2
Examine the dalil
The text states the ruling comes from a specific narration (nas) for the elderly; others like sick or traveler are not included. The dalil is ahad, making the ruling wajib, not fard.
Thubut zanni, dalala zanni.
3
Understand the illa (effective cause)
The illa is permanent impotence (istimrar al-ajz) to fast. An objection that hardship is the illa is rejected; the text specifies the elderly in continuous decline.
Illa is jaliyyah, extracted by tahrir al-manat.
4
Note intra-Hanafi differences
Abu Yusuf allows half sa' per day; Abu Hanifa requires more. The mufta bihi view accommodates both, adopting the more lenient amount.
These differences affect amount, not the principle of fidya.
5
Apply the principle of substitution (khilafah)
Substitution requires continued inability; if the person later becomes able, fidya is nullified. Contrast with tayammum, where initial inability suffices.
This principle prevents invalidating past acts.

Source Text

وللشيخ الفاني وهو يفدى فقط أي له الفطر وعليه الفدية وليست على غيره من المريض والمسافر والحامل والمرضع لعدم ورود نص فيهم، ووروده في الشيخ الفاني وهو الذي كل يوم في نقص إلى أن يموت وسمي به إما لأنه قرب من الفناء أو لأنه فنيت قوته، وإنما لزمته باعتبار شهوده للشهر حتى لو تحمل المشقة وصام كان مؤدياً، وإنما أبيح له الفطر لأجل الحرج وعذره ليس بعرض الزوال حتى يصار إلى القضاء فوجب الفدية لكل يوم نصف صاع أو صاعاً من تمر أو شعير كصدقة الفطر لكن يجوز هنا طعام الإباحة أكلتان من بر أو زبيب مشبعتان بخلاف صدقة الفطر كما قدمناه كذا في فتح القدير وفتاوى قاضيخان. وفي معراج الدراية : ولا يجوز في الفدية الإباحة لأنها تنبئ عن تمليك ا هـ. وهو مخالف لما قدمناه، ويحمل ما في المعراج على الفدية في الحج. ولو قدر على الصوم يبطل حكم الفداء لأن شرط الخلفية استمرار العجز في الصوم، وإنما قيدنا به ليخرج إذا قدر على الماء لا تبطل الصلوات المؤداة بالتيمم لأن خلفية التيمم مشروط بمجرد العجز عن الماء لا بقيد دوامه، وكذا خلفية الأشهر عن الأقراء في الاعتداد مشروط بانقطاع الدم من سن اليأس لا بشرط دوامه حتى لا تبطل الأنكحة الماضية بعود الدم على ما قدمناه في الحيض. وفي الكافي : وشرط الخلفية استمرار العجز كما في اليمين وفي صوم دم المتعة وغيرها قد تخلف لقيام الدليل ا هـ . وأشار المصنف فيما سبق من أن المسافر إذا لم يدرك عة فلا شيء عليه إذا مات إلى أن الشيخ الفاني لو كان مسافراً فمات قبل الإقامة لا يجب عليه بايصاء بالفدية لأنه يخالف غيره في التخفيف لا في التغليظ لكن ذكره الشارحون بصيغة قبل« ينبغي أن لا يجب مع أن الأولى الجزم به لاستفادته مما ذكرناه ولعلها ليست صريحة في كلام أهل المذهب فلم يجزموا بها، لأن الفدية لا تجوز إلا عن صوم هو أصل بنفسه لا بدل عن غيره فجازت عن رمضان وقضائه والنذر حتى لو نذر الأبد فضعف عن الصوم لاشتغاله بالمعيشة له أن يطعم ويفطر لأنه استيقن أن لا يقدر على قضائه وإن لم يقدر على الإطعام لعسرته يستغفر الله تعالى، وإن لم يقدر لشدة الحر كان له أن يفطر ويقضيه في الشتاء إذا لم يكن نذر الأبد. ولو نذر صوماً معيناً فلم يصم حتى صار فانياً جازت له الفدية، ولو وجبت عليه كفارة يمين أو قتل فلم يجد ما يكفر به وهو شيخ كبير عاجز عن الصوم أو لم يصم حتى صار شيخاً كبيراً لا تجوز له الفدية لأن الصوم هنا بدل عن غيره ولذا لا يجوز المصير إلى الصوم إلا عند العجز عما يكفر به من المال. كذا في فتح القدير وفي فتاوى قاضيخان وغاية البيان: وكذا لو حلق رأسه وهو محرم عن أذى ولم يجد نسكاً يذبحه ولا ثلاثة آصع حنطة يفرقها على ستة مساكين وهو فان لا يستطيع الصيام فأطعم عن الصيام لم يجز لأنه بدل. وفي القنية : ولو تصدق الشيخ الفاني بالليل عن صوم الفدية يجزئه . وفي فتاوى أبي حفص الكبير : إن شاء أعطى الفدية في أول رمضان بمرة وإن شاء أعطاها في آخره بمرة. وعن أبي يوسف: لو أعطى نصف صاع من برعن عن يوم واحد لمساكين يجوز . قال الحسن : وبه نأخذ وإن أعطى مسكيناً صاعاً عن يومين فعن أبي يوسف روايتان. وعند أبي حنيفة لا يجزئه كالإطعام في كفارة اليمين. وفي الفتاوى الظهيرية : استشهاداً لكون البدل لا بدل له. وذكر الصدر الشهيد رأسه مجروحاً فربط الجبيرة لم يجب عليه أن يمسح لأن المسح هنا أصل منصوص إذا كان جميع عليه لا بدل عن غيره ا هـ
And for the decrepit old man, he breaks the fast and only pays compensation, meaning he is allowed to break the fast and must pay compensation, and it is not required of others like the sick, traveler, pregnant, or nursing woman because there is no text regarding them, and the text exists for the decrepit old man who is in decline every day until he dies, and he is called that either because he approaches annihilation or because his strength has perished. It is only obligatory on him due to his witnessing the month, so if he bears hardship and fasts, he has performed it properly. He is permitted to break the fast due to hardship, and his excuse is not temporary so that he would have to make up the fast, so compensation is required for each day: half a sa' or a sa' of dates or barley like zakat al-fitr, but here it is permissible to give food of allowance, two satiating meals of wheat or raisins, unlike zakat al-fitr as we have mentioned, as in Fath al-Qadir and Fatawa Qadikhan. In Miraj al-Diraya: it is not permissible to give allowance in compensation because it implies possession, which contradicts what we have mentioned, and what is in Miraj is interpreted as compensation in Hajj. If he becomes able to fast, the ruling of compensation is nullified because the condition of substitution is the continuation of inability to fast. We qualified with this to exclude: if one becomes able to use water, the prayers performed with tayammum are not invalidated because substitution of tayammum is conditioned merely by inability to use water, not by its continuance; likewise, substitution of months for menstrual periods in waiting period is conditioned by cessation of blood from the age of menopause, not by its continuance, so past marriages are not invalidated by the return of blood as we mentioned in menstruation. In al-Kafi: the condition of substitution is the continuation of inability, as in the case of an oath, and in fasting of tamattu' blood etc., it may be overridden due to the existence of evidence. The author indicated in the preceding that if a traveler does not catch [the excuse?] there is nothing on him if he dies, and that if the decrepit old man is a traveler and dies before settling, he is not obligated to bequeath compensation because he differs from others in leniency not severity, but the commentators mentioned it with the wording 'it should not be obligatory', whereas the first view is to assert it due to what we mentioned, and perhaps it is not explicit in the words of the madhhab scholars so they did not assert it. Because compensation is only valid for a fast that is itself an original obligation, not a substitute for another, so it is valid for Ramadan, its make-up, and vows; even if he vowed perpetual fasting and weakened due to livelihood, he may feed and break because he is certain he cannot make it up, and if he cannot afford feeding due to hardship, he seeks forgiveness from Allah. If unable due to intense heat, he may break and make it up in winter if the vow was not perpetual. If he vowed a specific fast and did not fast until he became decrepit, compensation is permissible for him. If an oath or murder expiation becomes obligatory on him and he cannot find means to expiate and is an old man unable to fast, or did not fast until he became an old man, compensation is not permissible for him because the fast here is a substitute for another, and therefore resorting to fasting is not permissible except when unable to expiate with wealth. As in Fath al-Qadir and Fatawa Qadikhan and Ghayat al-Bayan: likewise, if he shaved his head while in ihram due to harm and could not find a sacrifice to slaughter nor three sa's of wheat to distribute to six poor people, and he is decrepit and unable to fast, and he feeds for the fast, it is not valid because it is a substitute. In al-Qunyah: if the decrepit old man gives charity at night for the fasting compensation, it suffices. In Fatawa Abu Hafs al-Kabir: if he wishes, he may give the compensation once at the beginning of Ramadan, or if he wishes, at the end. From Abu Yusuf: if he gives half a sa' of wheat for one day to poor persons, it is permissible. Al-Hasan said: we adopt this; if he gives a sa' to a poor person for two days, from Abu Yusuf there are two narrations. According to Abu Hanifa, it does not suffice him, like feeding in oath expiation. In al-Fatawa al-Zahiriyyah: as evidence that a substitute has no substitute. Al-Sadr al-Shahid mentioned: if his head is wounded and he ties a bandage, he is not obligated to wipe because wiping here is an original text if all of it is [covered], it is not a substitute for another.
Source pages p. 501

Commentary
This passage is a detailed ruling from a Hanafi fiqh commentary regarding the elderly person who is physically declining (shaykh fani) and cannot fast. The commentator begins by explaining that the base text states this person may break the fast and must only pay fidya (compensation), not make up the fasts. This ruling is specific to the elderly who are irretrievably declining; other individuals like the sick, traveler, pregnant, or nursing woman have different rulings—they must make up fasts if the excuse is temporary. The proof is the textual evidence (nas) specific to the elderly. The commentator then defines 'shaykh fani' as someone whose strength diminishes daily until death. The obligation of fidya is based on the fact that this person witnessed the month of Ramadan; if he chooses to bear hardship and fast, it is valid. But he is permitted to break due to hardship, and since his excuse is not temporary, qada (making up fasts) is not required, so fidya becomes obligatory. The amount of fidya is half a sa' or a sa' of dates or barley, similar to zakat al-fitr, but with the difference that it can be given as two satiating meals of wheat or raisins. There is a difference of opinion about allowing the 'ibaha (giving of food without ownership) in fidya; the commentator clarifies that the view in Miraj al-Diraya prohibiting it is overridden by other sources and applies to the fidya of Hajj. A key principle discussed is that the substitution (khilafah) of fidya for fasting requires the continuation of inability to fast. If the person later becomes able, the fidya ruling is nullified, unlike tayammum where the condition is initial inability. The commentator also discusses cases where the elderly person was also a traveler, suggesting that if he dies before settling, fidya may not be obligatory because the leniency of travel does not combine with severity. However, this is not conclusively established in the madhhab. Further, fidya is only valid for original fasting obligations (like Ramadan, make-up, vows), not for fasting that is itself a substitute for something else, such as expiation for oath or murder, because those fasts are badal (substitute) and a substitute cannot have a substitute. The passage then presents various rulings on the method of giving fidya, including permissibility of giving it at night, giving all at once, and the size of each payment. The commentary concludes with an analogous case from ihram to illustrate the principle that the substitute does not have a substitute.

Key Terms
الشيخ الفاني (al-shaykh al-fani): The elderly person who is in physical decline every day until death, permanently unable to fast.
الفدية (al-fidya): Compensation payment of food for each missed fast, obligatory on the elderly instead of qada.
الخلفية (al-khilafiyya): The principle of substitution where one act replaces another under certain conditions.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) The inability to fast must be continuous (mustamirr) until death.
C) The elderly person must also be a traveler.
D) The fidya must be given in the form of money.

Key Takeaway
The elderly with permanent inability pay fidya without qada; a substitute cannot have a substitute.

Breaking a Voluntary Fast: Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on breaking voluntary fast

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two narrations regarding breaking a voluntary fast, identify the mufta bihi position, and explain the rationale for preferring Abu Yusuf's view.

Core Idea
A voluntary fast becomes binding once started; the stronger view allows breaking with qada.

This passage addresses a key intra-Hanafi dispute: may a voluntary faster break his fast without a valid excuse? The apparent narration (zahir al-riwayah) prohibits it, but a narration from Abu Yusuf permits it with the obligation to make up (qada). The author and many later scholars prefer Abu Yusuf's view due to stronger evidence. We will analyze the competing positions and the rationale for tarjih.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two narrations
The passage mentions a narration from Abu Yusuf that allows breaking without excuse, and the apparent narration (zahir al-riwaya) that requires an excuse.
2
Understand the ruling of each
Under Abu Yusuf's narration: breaking is permissible but qada is required. Under zahir al-riwaya: breaking without excuse is sinful.
3
Examine the tarjih
The author and scholars like the investigator of Fath al-Qadir prefer Abu Yusuf's narration because the evidence is stronger and consistent.
4
Apply the mufta bihi
The operative position for fatwa is that a voluntary faster may break but must make up the fast (qada).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (وللمتطوع بغير عذر في رواية ويقضي أي له الفطر بعذر وبغيره، وإذا أفطر قضى إن كان نفلاً قصدياً وهذه الرواية عن أبي يوسف وظاهر الرواية أنه ليس له الفطر إلا من عذر. لا يصحح .. وصححه في المحيط. وإنما اقتصر على هذه الرواية لأنها أرجح من جهة الدليل ولهذا اختارها المحقق في فتح القدير وقال : إن الأدلة تظافرت عليها وهي أوجه. ثم اختلف المشايخ على ظاهر الرواية هل الضيافة عذر أو لا؟ قيل نعم، وقيل لا، وقيل عذر قبل الزوال بعده إلا إذا كان في عدم الفطر بعده عقوق لأحد الوالدين لا غيرهما حتى لو حلف عليه رجل بالطلاق الثلاث ليفطرن لا يفطر . وقيل : إن كان صاحب الطعام يرضى بمجرد حضوره وإن لم يأكل لا يباح الفطر، وإن كان يتأذى بذلك يفطر . كذا في فتح القدير. ولم شيئاً كما ترى. وفي الكافي والأظهر أنها عذر وصحح قاضيخان في شرح الجامع الصغير من أحكام الخلوة أن الضيافة عذر. وفي الفتاوى الظهيرية قالوا: والصحيح من المذهب أنه ينظر في ذلك إن كان صاحب الدعوة ممن يرضى بمجرد حضوره ولا يتأذى بترك الإفطار لا يفطر. وقال شمس الأئمة الحلواني : أحسن ما قيل في هذا الباب أنه إن كان يثق من نفسه القضاء يفطر دفعاً للأذى عن أخيه المسلم، وإن كان لا يثق لا يفطر وإن كان في ترك الإفطار أذى أخيه المسلم. وفي مسألة اليمين يجب أن يكون الجواب على هذا التفصيل ا هـ. وفي موضع آخر منها : وإن كان صائماً عن قضاء رمضان يكره له أن يفطر لأن له حكم رمضان ا هـ. ولهذا لا يفطر لو حلف رجل بالطلاق ليفطرن كذا في المحيط. وفي النهاية : الأظهر أن الضيافة عذر. وفي البزازية : لو حلف بطلاق امرأته إن لم يفطر أن نفلاً أفطر وإن قضاء لا والاعتماد على أنه يفطر فيهما ولا يحنثه، وإذا قلنا بأن الضيافة عذر في التطوع تكون عذراً في حق الضيف والمضيف. كذا في شرح الوقاية وأطلق في قضاء التطوع فشمل ما إذا كان فطره
His saying: 'And for the voluntary faster without an excuse in a narration, and he makes up' meaning he may break the fast with an excuse or without, and when he breaks he makes up if it was a voluntary fast with intention. This narration is from Abu Yusuf, and the apparent narration (zahir al-riwaya) is that he may not break except for an excuse. ... and he (the commentator) restricted himself to this narration because it is stronger in terms of evidence, and thus the investigator in Fath al-Qadir chose it and said: the evidences are consistent with it and it is weightier. Then the scholars differed regarding the apparent narration: Is hospitality an excuse or not? Some said yes, some said no, some said it is an excuse before noon only, unless refraining from breaking after noon would cause disobedience to parents, and no one else, so that even if a man swears by triple divorce that he must break, he does not break. And it was said: if the host is satisfied with just his presence even if he does not eat, breaking is not permissible; but if he is hurt by that, he breaks. As in Fath al-Qadir. And the end: nothing as you see. In al-Kafi: the apparent view is that it is an excuse, and Qadikhan in his commentary on al-Jami' al-Saghir from the rulings of seclusion corrected that hospitality is an excuse. In al-Fatawa al-Zahiriyya they said: the correct view of the madhhab is that one looks at this: if the host is one who is satisfied with just his presence and is not hurt by refraining from breaking, he does not break. Shams al-A'imma al-Hulwani said: the best that has been said on this topic is that if he is confident of being able to make up, he breaks to remove harm from his Muslim brother; if he is not confident, he does not break even if refraining causes harm to his Muslim brother. In the case of an oath, the answer must be according to this detail. In another place: if he is fasting to make up Ramadan, it is disliked for him to break because it has the ruling of Ramadan. Therefore, he does not break even if a man swears by divorce that he must break, as in al-Muhit. In al-Nihaya: the apparent view is that hospitality is an excuse. In al-Bazzaziyya: if he swears by divorce of his wife that he must break, if it is a voluntary fast he breaks, but if it is a make-up fast, no; and the reliance is that he breaks in both and does not incur the oath. And if we say that hospitality is an excuse in voluntary fasts, it is an excuse for both the guest and the host. As in Sharh al-Wiqaya. And he spoke generally in making up a voluntary fast, so it includes when his breaking...
Source pages p. 502

Commentary
This passage deals with the ruling for a person performing a voluntary (nafl) fast who breaks it. The base text states that according to one narration (from Abu Yusuf), the voluntary faster may break the fast with or without an excuse, and must make it up (qada) if he broke it intentionally (since he intended a specific voluntary fast). This is the preferred view according to the author, because the evidence supports it, and it is chosen in Fath al-Qadir. However, the apparent narration (zahir al-riwayah) of the madhhab is that a voluntary faster may not break the fast except for a valid excuse. The commentator then discusses the opinions of later scholars on whether hospitality (diyafah) is a valid excuse for breaking a voluntary fast. Several views are presented: (1) Hospitality is always an excuse; (2) It is only an excuse before noon; (3) It depends on whether the host would be hurt if the guest does not eat. The commentator also notes that if refraining from breaking after noon would cause disobedience to parents, then it is an excuse; otherwise, even a triple divorce oath does not obligate breaking. Further details: if the host is satisfied with mere presence, breaking is not allowed; if the host is hurt, breaking is allowed. Shams al-A'imma al-Hulwani gave a nuanced opinion: if the faster is confident he can make up the fast later, he should break to avoid harming the host; if not confident, he should not break, even if harm results. For make-up fasts of Ramadan, it is disliked to break due to the sanctity of Ramadan. The passage ends with a ruling from al-Bazzaziyya: if someone swears by divorce that he will break his fast, and it is a voluntary fast, he should break to avoid the oath; if it is a make-up fast, he should not break. The reliance is that he breaks in both cases and does not incur the oath.

Key Terms
المتطوع (al-mutatawwi'): A person performing a voluntary (nafl) fast intended by a specific intention (qasdi).
الضيافة (al-diyafah): Hospitality; being invited to eat by a host.
ظاهر الرواية (zahir al-riwayah): The transmitted ruling from the founding imams (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad) in the six authoritative books.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the preferred view in the Hanafi school, what is the ruling for a voluntary faster who breaks his fast without a valid excuse?
A) It is permissible and no qada is required.
B) It is permissible but qada is required.
C) It is sinful and qada is required.
D) It is sinful and no qada is required.

Key Takeaway
The mufta bihi in the Hanafi school is that a voluntary faster may break his fast without an excuse, but must make it up (qada) on another day.

Hospitality as an Excuse for Breaking a Voluntary Fast
Discussion of hospitality as excuse for breaking voluntary fast

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the various opinions on whether hospitality (diyafah) is a valid excuse for breaking a voluntary fast, and apply the preferred view to a given scenario.

Core Idea
Hospitality is a valid excuse for breaking a voluntary fast, subject to conditions regarding harm and confidence in making up.

After establishing the basic ruling, the passage explores a specific excuse: hospitality. The scholars differed widely on whether being a guest justifies breaking a voluntary fast, with conditions such as the host's feelings and the faster's ability to make up. This lesson examines these views and the preferred positions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the range of opinions
The passage lists several: hospitality is always an excuse; only before noon; only if the host would be hurt; only if the faster is confident of qada, etc.
2
Examine the condition of harm
The key factor is whether the host would be offended if the guest does not eat.
3
Consider the ability to make up
Shams al-A'imma al-Hulwani adds that confidence in qada is essential.
4
Apply to oaths and other cases
The passage also covers when an oath is involved, and distinguishes between voluntary and make-up fasts.
